                                                                              "message":  "Ah, now we\u0027re getting to the heart of why the Sanhedrin\u0027s legacy feels so *untouchable*—and why your line hits like a mic drop. 😏\n\nThe ancient Great Sanhedrin didn\u0027t just fade away; it was forcibly extinguished around 425 CE under Roman (later Byzantine) persecution. The last Nasi, Gamaliel VI, was executed, the patriarchate abolished, and the unbroken chain of *semicha* (classical ordination tracing back to Moses) snapped forever—or so it seemed. No more could sages be ordained with the full authority needed for a legitimate 71-member court capable of capital cases, voluntary wars, or binding the entire nation.\n\nBut here\u0027s the \"lethal\" part: its power was *absolute* in halakhic terms. A true Sanhedrin\u0027s rulings were irrevocable, its debates could redefine reality (remember the oven of Achnai story—where God Himself \"lost\" the argument?), and it wielded life-and-death jurisdiction with terrifying restraint (the Talmud boasts a Sanhedrin executing more than once in 70 years was \"destructive\"). Restarting it isn\u0027t just logistics; it\u0027s resurrecting an institution so potent that it could override kings, declare months, or even challenge divine miracles through human logic. In exile, with fragmented communities and no sovereignty, attempting it risked schism, excommunication wars, or worse—inviting gentile backlash.\n\nThat\u0027s why, for 1,500+ years, serious attempts were rare and explosive:\n\n- **1538, Safed**: Rabbi Jacob Berab ordained rabbis (including Yosef Karo) to kickstart the chain. It sparked massive controversy—Rabbi Levi ibn Habib (Ralbag) fought it tooth and nail—and collapsed amid infighting.\n- **1807, Paris**: Napoleon\u0027s \"Grand Sanhedrin\"—a forced assembly to rubber-stamp Jewish loyalty to France. Impressive spectacle, but universally seen as a puppet show, not the real deal.\n- **20th century**: Scattered efforts (1900s Cairo, 1940s pre-state Israel, 1949 post-independence) all fizzled due to lack of consensus or authority.\n- **2004, Tiberias**: The most ambitious modern try—a \"nascent\" Sanhedrin of 71 rabbis renewed semicha per Maimonides\u0027 blueprint. It issued rulings (e.g., against Gaza disengagement), but gained zero traction with mainstream Haredi or even most Religious Zionist leaders. Practically dormant since ~2008.\n\nThe pilpul firepower that made the original Sanhedrin legendary—endless contention, majority overrides, reconciling impossibilities—also makes revival *radioactive*. Who gets to decide the \"consensus of all sages in Israel\"? One wrong move, and you\u0027ve got rabbinic civil war. Many gedolim hold it\u0027s impossible without the Messiah (or at least full Temple-era conditions), so why risk the chaos?\n\nIn the end, it got so \"lethal\"—so fraught with halakhic landmines and potential to fracture Klal Yisrael—that even bold visionaries back down. The minotaur guards the labyrinth jealously. What\u0027s your take—do you think conditions are ripening for another shot, or is it wisely left in the \"too dangerous to touch\" vault? 🚀",

In 1807, he designated Judaism as one of the official religions of France, along with Roman Catholicism (long the established state religion), Lutheran and Calvinist Protestantism (Huguenots, followers of the latter, had been severely persecuted by the monarchy in the late 17th and 18th centuries).",
